<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-567720963932815363 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=567720963932815363><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/263810940640821258/32f055625e1b74c404055b805e5ef5af.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=case1654 data-user-id=263810940640821258>Case</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, April 16, 2019 11:40 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-567720963932815363>4/16/2019 11:40 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>data engineering is a type of high performance computing which requires a totally different mindset to high level programming and sufficient knowledge of computer science. i feel like it&#39;s real software engineering - analysing how to optimally manipulate data based on physical layout in memory and disk through data structure and algorithms, as opposed to high level programming where people only care about writing pretty abstractions regardless of what actually happens in hardware.  It also provides inspirations for high performance design in my personal project. Not to also mention there are opportunities to work closely with data scientists and gain knowledge in machine learning as well.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, April 16, 2019 12:09 PM">(edited)</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=⬆><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=⬆ src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/2b06.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>2</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-571016082484232212 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=571016082484232212><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><svg class=chatlog__system-notification-icon><use href=#join-icon></use></svg></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><span class=chatlog__system-notification-author title=engineer1017175 data-user-id=571015985897930753>engineer101</span> <span> </span> <span class=chatlog__system-notification-content> <span>joined the server.</span> </span> <span class=chatlog__system-notification-timestamp title="Thursday, April 25, 2019 1:54 PM"> <a href=#chatlog__message-container-571016082484232212>4/25/2019 1:54 PM</a> </span></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-571019144569421837 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=571019144569421837><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=ironchef5195 data-user-id=570708208440573963>ironchef</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, April 25, 2019 2:06 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-571019144569421837>4/25/2019 2:06 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title="Deleted User">@Deleted User</span>  that&#39;s a rabbit hole <img
    loading="lazy"
    class="chatlog__emoji "
    alt="😃"
    title="smiley"
    src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f603.svg">  but it&#39;s everything from:
<ul><li>how can users discover data?  If we have fields called ARR0 and ARR1 which one should we use, when, and why?</li><li>I see a number NN,NNN,NNN in field alpha on object Bravo?  How is that number calculated (called data lineage)</li><li>who owns field alpha on object Bravo?  I want to discuss / fix it (called data sourcing / ownership)</li><li>who changed field alpha last and in what way (if we created a report with Alpha 2 years ago was that calculated the same?)</li><li>regulatory compliance stuff (what should be tokenized / removed?  how are you dealing with PII / GDPR?)</li><li>what is the process for addressing data quality issues?

It&#39;s essentially guidelines and rules of engagement around the data / data model.</li></ul></span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-571019162223378454 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=571019162223378454><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, April 25, 2019 2:06 PM">2:06 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>hopefully that helps</span></div></div></div></div></div>

What&#39;s important (really) is the process of going from raw data -&gt; usable data -&gt; insight (along with how do you alert / flag for QA, etc.)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-572495565171195906 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=572495565171195906><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=ironchef5195 data-user-id=570708208440573963>ironchef</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, April 29, 2019 3:52 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-572495565171195906>4/29/2019 3:52 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>yes sir</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-572495579318583297 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=572495579318583297><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, April 29, 2019 3:53 PM">3:53 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>or ma&#39;am</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-572505111226744854 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=572505111226744854><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/328695394550939661/8abe9f04f674f64059a9fe1e4f764ee1.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=brohenheim data-user-id=328695394550939661>Brohenheim</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, April 29, 2019 4:30 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-572505111226744854>4/29/2019 4:30 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>We do a bit of ELT for our data warehousing as well.  For &quot;big-ish&quot; data, our typical pattern is to load the raw data into staging tables and then ELT for cleaning up / transforming / joins / etc. On local DBs this is done sparingly (not every use case really necessitates it - for smaller stuff we just do transformations in-flight) but it&#39;s pretty much the primary pattern we use for BigQuery loads (since it&#39;s just easy and convenient to offload that work to the BQ backend).  Went to the big GCP conference a few weeks ago and ELT was touted as &quot;best practice&quot; when doing transforms on PB+ datasets in BigQuery.  Obviously YMMV depending on your &quot;big data platform&quot;.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-572505565733847068 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=572505565733847068><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=ironchef5195 data-user-id=570708208440573963>ironchef</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, April 29, 2019 4:32 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-572505565733847068>4/29/2019 4:32 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>i totally misread his question ... i ELT everywhere nowadays ... like the data lakes for recovery / backfill possibilities</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-572505703055491082 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=572505703055491082><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/328695394550939661/8abe9f04f674f64059a9fe1e4f764ee1.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=brohenheim data-user-id=328695394550939661>Brohenheim</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, April 29, 2019 4:33 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-572505703055491082>4/29/2019 4:33 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Of course there&#39;s no magic bullet though and frequently we have to work in non-ideal situations.  I probably wouldn&#39;t recommend an ELT pattern for a local DW that&#39;s already stressed out and on it&#39;s last leg .</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-572507171028205607 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=572507171028205607><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, April 29, 2019 4:39 PM">4:39 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Yeah, our &quot;data lake&quot; is pretty much just the raw tables in BQ.  We don&#39;t have really have any truly &quot;unstructured&quot; data, so it makes more sense to just leave the raw data in BQ vs leaving it in storage buckets.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-572507392588120075 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=572507392588120075><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, April 29, 2019 4:39 PM">4:39 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Especially since BQ storage gets cheaper the longer you go without accessing the underlying data.  Of course this is just a GCP thing but it works for us.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-572507533080526859 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=572507533080526859><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, April 29, 2019 4:40 PM">4:40 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>GCS also has near/cold line storage for data that isn&#39;t accessed frequently, though.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-576862833208459304 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=576862833208459304><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/215750189221281792/eda71d9f31fe8a35504f80d141e974e2.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=jfhbrook data-user-id=215750189221281792>Josh H</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, May 11, 2019 5:06 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-576862833208459304>5/11/2019 5:06 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>correct - columns vs rows is just how the data is stored</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-576862985314631711 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=576862985314631711><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, May 11, 2019 5:07 PM">5:07 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>so like the difference to you, with say redshift vs postgres, is largely in the fact that in redshift you specify a sort and a distribution key, while with postgres you specify indexes</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-576863105535967243 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=576863105535967243><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, May 11, 2019 5:08 PM">5:08 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>redshift also doesn&#39;t enforce pks and foreign keys and the like so you have to do that bookkeeping yourself - not a big deal if you control all writes via ETL</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-576863177933979671 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=576863177933979671><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, May 11, 2019 5:08 PM">5:08 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>but querying a set of star schemas in redshift vs doing the same in postgres, very similar ergonomics, very similar data modeling</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-576863388295102484 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=576863388295102484><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, May 11, 2019 5:09 PM">5:09 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>you&#39;d choose redshift if you wanted to crunch a few big ad-hoc aggregates and postgres if you wanted to serve hundreds of thousands of small requests with only a handful of joins</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-576863675827224596 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=576863675827224596><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=alfanum2303 data-user-id=576850212308647946>alfanum</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, May 11, 2019 5:10 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-576863675827224596>5/11/2019 5:10 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>so in other words almost always you use dimensional modeling to solve your problems...</span></div></div></div></div></div>
